      "cell_type": "markdown",
      "source": "**Big Data Project: Film recommendation engine using the IMDb 5000 dataset**\n\nThis project aims at recommending movies, TV shows based on user's preference of the previous movies and TV shows. We use the IMDb 5000 dataset having movies.csv and credits.csv dataset files.\nBasically the user would select a movie and based on that movie alone the recommendation engine would suggest 5 movies that the user may prefer. The selection, of course, is based on three categories\n* **popularity-based engine** - The most impersonal recommendation engine as it doesn't consider the user's preference.\n* **content-based engine** - Recommends other movies based on the description of the current movie.\n* **collaborative-based engine** - Recommends movies based on other users' choice whose previous list of movies included the user's current movie."
    },
    {
      "metadata": {
        "_uuid": "5208f6b68a269f05c1546bff32f8b532eb872987"

      "cell_type": "markdown",
      "source": "Some information about the used packages\n\n1. **numpy**: A library for the Python programming language, adding support for large, multi-dimensional arrays and matrices, along with a large collection of high-level mathematical functions to operate on these arrays. \nThe core functionality of NumPy is its \"ndarray\", for n-dimensional array, data structure. These arrays are strided views on memory. In contrast to Python's built-in list data structure (which, despite the name, is a dynamic array), these arrays are homogeneously typed: all elements of a single array must be of the same type. Such arrays can also be views into memory buffers allocated by C/C++, Cython, and Fortran extensions to the CPython interpreter without the need to copy data around, giving a degree of compatibility with existing numerical libraries. \n\n\n*Source: [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NumPy)*\n\n\n2. **json**: The json library can parse JSON from strings or files. The library parses JSON into a Python dictionary or list. It can also convert Python dictionaries or lists into JSON strings. *Source: [Python Guide](http://docs.python-guide.org/en/latest/scenarios/json/)*\n\n\n3. **matplotlib**: Matplotlib is a Python 2D plotting library which produces publication quality figures in a variety of hardcopy formats and interactive environments across platforms. Matplotlib can be used in Python scripts, the Python and IPython shells, the Jupyter notebook, web application servers, and four graphical user interface toolkits.\nMatplotlib is a numerical mathematics extension NumPy. It provides an object-oriented API for embedding plots into applications using general-purpose GUI toolkits like Tkinter, wxPython, Qt, or GTK+. There is also a procedural \"pylab\" interface based on a state machine (like OpenGL), designed to closely resemble that of MATLAB, though its use is discouraged. SciPy makes use of matplotlib. \n\n\n*Source: [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matplotlib)*\n\n\n4. **pandas**: pandas is a software library written for the Python programming language for data manipulation and analysis. In particular, it offers data structures and operations for manipulating numerical tables and time series. It is free software released under the three-clause BSD license. The name is derived from the term \"panel data\", an econometrics term for data sets that include observations over multiple time periods for the same individuals. \n\n\n*Source: [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pandas_(software))*\n\n\n5. **matplotlib.pyplot**: is a collection of command style functions that make matplotlib work like MATLAB. Each pyplot function makes some change to a figure: e.g., creates a figure, creates a plotting area in a figure, plots some lines in a plotting area, decorates the plot with labels, etc. In matplotlib.pyplot various states are preserved across function calls, so that it keeps track of things like the current figure and plotting area, and the plotting functions are directed to the current axes (please note that “axes” here and in most places in the documentation refers to the axes part of a figure and not the strict mathematical term for more than one axis).\n\n\n*Source: [Maplotlib.org](https://matplotlib.org/users/pyplot_tutorial.html)*\n\n\n6. **seaborn**: Seaborn is a Python visualization library based on matplotlib. It provides a high-level interface for drawing attractive statistical graphics. Seaborn aims to make visualization a central part of exploring and understanding data. The plotting functions operate on dataframes and arrays containing a whole dataset and internally perform the necessary aggregation and statistical model-fitting to produce informative plots. If matplotlib “tries to make easy things easy and hard things possible”, seaborn tries to make a well-defined set of hard things easy too.\n\n\n*Source: [seaborn.pydata.org](https://seaborn.pydata.org/)*\n\n\n7. **math**: This module is always available. It provides access to the mathematical functions defined by the C standard.\nThese functions cannot be used with complex numbers; use the functions of the same name from the cmath module if you require support for complex numbers. The distinction between functions which support complex numbers and those which don’t is made since most users do not want to learn quite as much mathematics as required to understand complex numbers. Receiving an exception instead of a complex result allows earlier detection of the unexpected complex number used as a parameter, so that the programmer can determine how and why it was generated in the first place.\n\n\n*Source: [python.org](https://docs.python.org/2/library/math.html)*\n\n\n8. **nltk**: NLTK is a leading platform for building Python programs to work with human language data. It provides easy-to-use interfaces to over 50 corpora and lexical resources such as WordNet, along with a suite of text processing libraries for classification, tokenization, stemming, tagging, parsing, and semantic reasoning and wrappers for industrial-strength NLP libraries. NLTK is intended to support research and teaching in NLP or closely related areas, including empirical linguistics, cognitive science, artificial intelligence, information retrieval, and machine learning. NLTK has been used successfully as a teaching tool, as an individual study tool, and as a platform for prototyping and building research systems. There are 32 universities in the US and 25 countries using NLTK in their courses. NLTK supports classification, tokenization, stemming, tagging, parsing, and semantic reasoning functionalities.\n\n\n*Source: [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_Language_Toolkit)*\n\n\n\n9. **warnings**: Warning messages are typically issued in situations where it is useful to alert the user of some condition in a program, where that condition (normally) doesn’t warrant raising an exception and terminating the program. For example, one might want to issue a warning when a program uses an obsolete module.  There are two stages in warning control: first, each time a warning is issued, a determination is made whether a message should be issued or not; next, if a message is to be issued, it is formatted and printed using a user-settable hook.\n\n\n*Source: [python.org](https://docs.python.org/2/library/warnings.html)*\n\n\nLoading the movies and credit dataset that will be used throughout this notebook"

linear algebra\nimport pandas as pd # data processing, CSV file I/O (e.g. pd.read_csv)\n\n# Input data files are available in the \"../input/\" directory.\n# For example, running this (by clicking run or pressing Shift+Enter) will list the files in the input directory\n\nimport os\nprint(os.listdir(\"../input\"))\n\nimport json\nimport pandas as pd\n\nLOST_COLUMNS = [\n    'actor_1_facebook_likes',\n    'actor_2_facebook_likes',\n    'actor_3_facebook_likes',\n    'aspect_ratio',\n    'cast_total_facebook_likes',\n    'color',\n    'content_rating',\n    'director_facebook_likes',\n    'facenumber_in_poster',\n    'movie_facebook_likes',\n    'movie_imdb_link',\n    'num_critic_for_reviews',\n    'num_user_for_reviews']\n#____________________________________\ntmdbToIMDb = {\n    'budget': 'budget',\n    'genres': 'genres',\n    'revenue': 'gross',\n    'title': 'movie_title',\n    'runtime': 'duration',\n    'original_language': 'language',\n    'keywords': 'plot_keywords',\n    'vote_count': 'num_voted_users'}\n\nIMDB_COLUMNS_TO_REMAP = {'imdb_score': 'vote_average'}\n\n# Load tmdb_movies dataset\ndef loadTMDbMovies(path):\n    #using pandas\n    movieData = pd.read_csv(path)\n    movieData['release_date'] = pd.to_datetime(movieData['release_date']).apply(lambda x: x.date())\n    columns = ['genres', 'keywords', 'production_countries','production_companies', 'spoken_languages']\n    for column in columns:\n        #using json\n        movieData[column] = movieData[column].apply(json.loads)\n    #endfor\n    return movieData\n#endmethod\n\n# Loads tmdb_credits dataset\ndef loadTMDbCredits(path):\n    #using pandas\n    creditData = pd.read_csv(path)\n    columns = ['cast', 'crew']\n    for column in columns:\n        #using json\n        creditData[column] = creditData[column].apply(json.loads)\n    #endfor\n    return creditData\n#endmethod\n# Any results you write to the current directory are saved as output.",

      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "def convertToOriginalFormat(movies, credits):\n    #using import pandas as pd\n    tmdbMovies = movies.copy()\n    tmdbMovies.rename(columns = tmdbToIMDb, inplace =  True)\n    tmdbMovies['title_year'] = pd.to_datetime(tmdbMovies['release_date']).apply(lambda x: x.year)\n    tmdbMovies['country'] = tmdbMovies['production_countries'].apply(lambda x: safeAccess(x, [0, 'name']))\n    tmdbMovies['language'] = tmdbMovies['spoken_languages'].apply(lambda x: safeAccess(x, [0, 'name']))\n    tmdbMovies['genres'] = tmdbMovies['genres'].apply(pipeFlattenNames)\n    tmdbMovies['plot_keywords'] = tmdbMovies['plot_keywords'].apply(pipeFlattenNames)\n    tmdbMovies['director_name'] = credits['crew'].apply(getDirector)\n    tmdbMovies['actor_1_name'] = credits['cast'].apply(lambda x: safeAccess(x, [1, 'name']))\n    tmdbMovies['actor_2_name'] = credits['cast'].apply(lambda x: safeAccess(x, [2, 'name']))\n    tmdbMovies['actor_3_name'] = credits['cast'].apply(lambda x: safeAccess(x, [3, 'name']))\n\n    return tmdbMovies\n#endmethod\n\ndef safeAccess(container, indexValues):\n    #Return missing value instead of an error upon indexing failure\n    #using import pandas as pd\n    result = container\n    try:\n        for i in indexValues:\n            result = result[i]\n        #endfor\n        return result\n    except IndexError or KeyError:\n        return pd.np.nan\n#endmethod\n\ndef pipeFlattenNames(keywords):\n    return '|'.join([x['name'] for x in keywords])\n#endmethod\n\ndef getDirector(crewData):\n    directors = [x['name'] for x in crewData if x['job'] == 'Director']\n    return safeAccess(directors, [0])\n#endmethod",

      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "def countWord(df, refCol, wordList):\n    keywordCount = dict()\n    for s in wordList: keywordCount[s] = 0\n    #endfor\n    for listOfKeywords in df[refCol].str.split('|'):\n        if type(listOfKeywords) == float and pd.isnull(listOfKeywords):continue\n        #endif\n        for s in [s for s in listOfKeywords if s in wordList]:\n            if pd.notnull(s): keywordCount[s] += 1\n            #endif\n        #endfor\n    #endfor\n    #Convert the dictionary into a list to sort the keywords by frequency\n    keywordOccurences = []\n    for key, value in keywordCount.items():\n        keywordOccurences.append([key, value])\n    #endfor\n    keywordOccurences.sort(key = lambda x:x[1], reverse = True)\n    return keywordOccurences, keywordCount\n#endmethod",

      "cell_type": "markdown",
      "source": "** Cleanup of data **\n\n\nClearly the plot_keywords is important feature of this dataset and there appears to be multiple synonyms that are quite similar to other keywords, for example: musicals and music, time traveller and time travel etc. These redundant keywords must be grouped under common roots. We collect all the keywords using the NLTK package.\n\n**The Natural Language Toolkit, or more commonly NLTK**, is a suite of libraries and programs for symbolic and statistical natural language processing (NLP) for English written in the Python programming language. It was developed by Steven Bird and Edward Loper in the Department of Computer and Information Science at the University of Pennsylvania.NLTK includes graphical demonstrations and sample data. It is accompanied by a book that explains the underlying concepts behind the language processing tasks supported by the toolkit, plus a cookbook.\n\n*Source: [Wikipedia](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/24647400/what-is-the-best-stemming-method-in-python)*\n\nHere are some examples using the PorterStemmer\n> import nltk\nps = nltk.stemmer.PorterStemmer()\nps.stem('grows')\n'grow'\nps.stem('leaves')\n'leav'\nps.stem('fairly')\n'fairli'"
    },
    {
      "metadata": {
        "_uuid": "311fc394ae4ea69bb16a98e6adaa2a7207938215"
      },
      "cell_type": "markdown",
      "source": "*Source: [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_Language_Toolkit)*\n\n\n> **nltk.wordnet.WordNetLemmatizer() and nltk.stem.PorterStemmer():**\nThe goal of both stemming and lemmatization is to reduce inflectional forms and sometimes derivationally related forms of a word to a common base form.\nHowever, the two words differ in their flavor. Stemming usually refers to a crude heuristic process that chops off the ends of words in the hope of achieving this goal correctly most of the time, and often includes the removal of derivational affixes. Lemmatization usually refers to doing things properly with the use of a vocabulary and morphological analysis of words, normally aiming to remove inflectional endings only and to return the base or dictionary form of a word, which is known as the lemma .\n\n\n**From the NLTK docs:**\n\n> Lemmatization and stemming are special cases of normalization. They identify a canonical representative for a set of related word forms."
    },

      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "def keywordsInventory(dataframe, colname = 'plot_keywords'):\n    PS = nltk.stem.PorterStemmer()\n    keywordsRoots = dict() # collect the words / root\n    keywordsSelect = dict() # association: root <-> keyword\n    categoryKeys = []\n    iCount = 0\n    for s in dataframe[colname]:\n        if pd.isnull(s): continue\n        #endif\n        for t in s.split('|'):\n            t = t.lower() ; racine = PS.stem(t)\n            if racine in keywordsRoots:\n                keywordsRoots[racine].add(t)\n            else:\n                keywordsRoots[racine] = { t }\n            #endif\n        #endfor\n    #endfor\n    for s in keywordsRoots.keys():\n        if len(keywordsRoots[s]) > 1:\n            minLength = 1000\n            for k in keywordsRoots[s]:\n                if len(k) < minLength:\n                    leaf = k ; minLength = len(k)\n                #endif\n            #endfor\n            categoryKeys.append(leaf)\n            keywordsSelect[s] = leaf\n        else:\n            categoryKeys.append(list(keywordsRoots[s])[0])\n            keywordsSelect[s] = list(keywordsRoots[s])[0]\n        #endif\n    #endfor\n    print(\"Number of keywords in variable '{}' : {}\".format(colname, len(categoryKeys)))\n    return categoryKeys, keywordsRoots, keywordsSelect\n#endmethod",
      "execution_count": 14,

    {
      "metadata": {
        "_uuid": "f174e26be5da2cffb9b67111b4ffa6854da33b07"
      },
      "cell_type": "markdown",
      "source": "** Recommendation engine**\n\n\nIn order to build the recommendation engine, we will basically proceed in two steps:\n\n1. determine  N  films with a content similar to the entry provided by the user\n\n2. select the 5 most popular films among these  N  films\n\n\n**Similarity**\n\nWhen builing the engine, the first step thus consists in defining a criteria that would tell us how close two films are. To do so, we start from the description of the film that was selected by the user: from it, we get the director name, the names of the actors and a few keywords. We then build a matrix where each row corresponds to a film of the database and where the columns correspond to the previous quantities (director + actors + keywords) plus the k genres.\n\nIn this matrix, the  aij  coefficients take either the value 0 or 1 depending on the correspondance between the significance of column  j  and the content of film  i . For exemple, if \"keyword 1\" is in film  i , we will have  aij  = 1 and 0 otherwise. Once this matrix has been defined, we determine the distance between two films according to:\n\n\n\\begin{eqnarray}\nd_{m, n} = \\sqrt{  \\sum_{i = 1}^{N} \\left( a_{m,i}  - a_{n,i} \\right)^2  } \n\\end{eqnarray}\n\n\n**Popularity based**\nAccording to similarities between entries, we get a list of  N  films. At this stage, we select 5 films from this list and, to do so, we give a score for every entry. we decide de compute the score according to 3 criteria:\n\n* the IMDB score\n* the number of votes the entry received\n* the year of release\n\n\nThe two first criteria will be a direct measure of the popularity of the various entries in IMDB. For the third criterium, we introduce the release year since the database spans films from the early  XXth  century up to now. We assume that people's favorite films will be most of the time from the same epoch.\n\nThen, we calculate the score according to the formula:\n\n\\begin{eqnarray}\n\\mathrm{score} = IMDB^2 \\times \\phi_{\\sigma_1, c_1} \\times  \\phi_{\\sigma_2, c_2}\n\\end{eqnarray}\n\nwhere  ϕ  is a gaussian function:\n\n\\begin{eqnarray}\n\\phi_{\\sigma, c}(x) \\propto \\mathrm{exp}\\left(-\\frac{(x-c)^2}{2 \\, \\sigma^2}\\right)\n\\end{eqnarray}\n\n\nFor votes, we get the maximum number of votes among the  N  films and we set  σ1=c1=m . For years, I put  σ1=20  and I center the gaussian on the title year of the film selected by the user. With the gaussians, we put more weight to the entries with a large number of votes and to the films whose release year is close to the title selected by the user."
    },
    {
      "metadata": {
        "_cell_guid": "c756c4a7-4376-4243-8ca6-e97ccc120532",
        "_uuid": "c0792edd59e8ea1cf2c73f640d536a1cbb486628",
        "collapsed": true,
        "trusted": true

      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "gaussianFilter = lambda x,y,sigma: math.exp(-(x-y)**2/(2*sigma**2))",

      "outputs": []

      "source": "The following function, **entryVariables**, returns values taken by variables 'director_name', 'actorN_name' wherre N => [1:3] and 'plot_keywords' for the film selected by the user."
    },
    {
      "metadata": {
        "_cell_guid": "a0ea2022-49be-4ccb-a5e3-35e1976cea6a",

      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "def entryVariables(df, idEntry):\n    colLabels = []\n    if pd.notnull(df['director_name'].iloc[idEntry]):\n        for s in df['director_name'].iloc[idEntry].split('|'):\n            colLabels.append(s)\n        #endfor\n    #endif\n    \n    for i in range(3):\n        column = 'actor_NUM_name'.replace('NUM', str(i + 1))\n        if pd.notnull(df[column].iloc[idEntry]):\n            for s in df[column].iloc[idEntry].split('|'):\n                colLabels.append(s)\n            #endfor\n        #endif\n    #endfor\n    \n    if pd.notnull(df['plot_keywords'].iloc[idEntry]):\n        for s in df['plot_keywords'].iloc[idEntry].split('|'):\n            colLabels.append(s)\n        #endfor\n    #endif\n    \n    return colLabels\n#endmethod",

      "source": "The following function, **addVariables** adds a list of variables to the dataframe given in input and initialize these variables at 0 or 1 depending on the correspondance with the description of the films and the content of the REF_VAR variable given in input."
    },
    {
      "metadata": {
        "_cell_guid": "0802e2f5-0e94-4f24-88e4-fc98c65c4141",
        "_uuid": "586a7fdeb24b89b62a874b63312f71788d80d9a6",
        "collapsed": true,
        "trusted": true

      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "def addVariables(df, REF_VAR):\n    for s in REF_VAR: df[s] = pd.Series([0 for _ in range(len(df))])\n    colnames = ['genres', 'actor_1_name', 'actor_2_name',\n                'actor_3_name', 'director_name', 'plot_keywords']\n    for col in colnames:\n        for index, row in df.iterrows():\n            if pd.isnull(row[col]): continue\n            #endif\n            for s in row[col].split('|'):\n                if s in REF_VAR: df.set_value(index, s, 1)\n                #endif\n            #endfor\n        #endfor\n    #endfor\n       \n    return df\n#endmethod",

      "cell_type": "markdown",
      "source": "The following function, **recommend**, creates a list of N (=31) films similar to the film selected by the user."
    },
    {
      "metadata": {
        "_cell_guid": "5bc3e3c2-34be-4787-bbfd-05f18ca05e53",
        "_uuid": "727e0cd4abee04019a9eebb162e3fb11e23c7a24",

      },
      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "def recommend(df, idEntry):\n    dfCopy = df.copy(deep = True)\n    listDF = set()\n    for s in df['genres'].str.split('|').values:\n        listDF = listDF.union(set(s))\n    #endfor\n    \n    #Creating additional variables to check the similarity\n    var = entryVariables(dfCopy, idEntry)\n    var += list(listDF)\n    dfNew = addVariables(dfCopy, var)\n    \n    #Calculating the nearest neighbours using current variable\n    x = dfNew.as_matrix(var)\n    near = NearestNeighbors(n_neighbors=31, algorithm = 'auto', metric = 'euclidean').fit(x)\n    distances, indices = near.kneighbors(x)\n    xTest = dfNew.iloc[idEntry].as_matrix(var)\n    xTest = xTest.reshape(1, -1)\n    distances, indices = near.kneighbors(xTest)\n    \n    return indices[0][:]\n#endmethod",
      "execution_count": 39,
      "outputs": []

      "cell_type": "markdown",
      "source": "The following function, **extractParameters** extracts some variables of the dataframe given in input and returns this list for a selection of N films. This list is ordered according to criteria established in the **critereSelection** function given below."
    },
    {
      "metadata": {
        "_cell_guid": "8900f541-dd90-474f-ad32-46a50554cb0f",
        "_uuid": "d2ca28b939790e556cb4e2460f5152ef8db3cbfe",
        "collapsed": true,
        "trusted": true
      },
      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "def extractParameters(df, listOfFilms):     \n    paraList = ['_' for _ in range(31)]\n    i = 0\n    maxUsers = -1\n    for index in listOfFilms:\n        paraList[i] = list(df.iloc[index][['movie_title', 'title_year',\n                                        'imdb_score', 'num_user_for_reviews', \n                                        'num_voted_users']])\n        paraList[i].append(index)\n        maxUsers = max(maxUsers, paraList[i][4] )\n        i += 1\n        \n    mainTitle = paraList[0][0]\n    annRef  = paraList[0][1]\n    paraList.sort(key = lambda x:critereSelection(mainTitle, maxUsers,\n                                    annRef, x[0], x[1], x[2], x[4]), reverse = True)\n\n    return paraList ",

      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "def sequel(title1, title2):\n    if fuzz.ratio(title1, title2) > 50 or fuzz.token_set_ratio(title1, title2) > 50:\n        return True\n    else:\n        return False\n    #endif\n#endmethod",

      "cell_type": "markdown",
      "source": "The following function, **critereSelection **, compares the 2 titles passed in input and defines if these titles are similar or not."
    },
    {
      "metadata": {
        "_cell_guid": "2e9a33e1-7d9f-4204-a04e-bf8a953f8801",
        "_uuid": "d17ab18721d87317f5cf78710087b6d27dce8246",
        "collapsed": true,
        "trusted": true
      },
      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "def critereSelection(mainTitle, maxUsers, annRef, title, ann, imdbScore, votes):\n    if pd.notnull(annRef):\n        fact1 = gaussianFilter(annRef, ann, 20)\n    else:\n        fact1 = 1\n    #endif\n    sigma = maxUsers * 1.0\n    \n    if pd.notnull(votes):\n        fact2 = gaussianFilter(votes, maxUsers, sigma)\n    else:\n        fact2 = 0\n    #endif\n    \n    if sequel(mainTitle, title):\n        note = 0\n    else:\n        note = imdbScore**2 * fact1 * fact2\n    #endif\n    \n    return note\n#endmethod",
      "execution_count": 42,
      "outputs": []
    },

      "source": "The following function, **addToSelection**, function complete the **filmSelect** list which contains 5 films that will be recommended to the user. The films are selected from the parametres_films list and are taken into account only if the title is different enough from other film titles."
    },
    {
      "metadata": {
        "_cell_guid": "6d6161c6-1b30-4656-8d1f-e1d01e9fca72",

      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "def addToSelection(filmSelect, paraList):\n    filmList = filmSelect[:]\n    iCount = len(filmList)\n    for i in range(31):\n        isInList = False\n        for s in filmSelect:\n            if s[0] == paraList[i][0]: isInList = True\n            #endif\n            if sequel(paraList[i][0], s[0]): isInList = True\n            #endif\n        #endfor\n        \n        if isInList: continue\n        #endif\n        iCount += 1\n        if iCount <= 5:\n            filmList.append(paraList[i])\n        #endif\n    #endfor\n    return filmList\n#endmethod",
      "execution_count": 43,
      "outputs": []

      "cell_type": "markdown",
      "source": "The following function, **removeSequel** removes sequels from the list if more that two films from a serie are present. The older one is kept."
    },
    {
      "metadata": {
        "_cell_guid": "a6d406b4-426a-4ac0-9d85-eee8342beff8",
        "_uuid": "b32fe50fe9a7ee144f794b6d9cbdb3f3cf313523",
        "collapsed": true,
        "trusted": true
      },
      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "def removeSequel(filmSelect):\n    remove = []\n    for i, film_1 in enumerate(filmSelect):\n        for j, film_2 in enumerate(filmSelect):\n            if j <= i: continue\n            #endif\n            if sequel(film_1[0], film_2[0]):\n                lastFilm = film_2[0] if film_1[1] < film_2[1] else film_1[0]\n                remove.append(lastFilm)\n            #endif\n        #endfor\n    #endfor\n    filmList = [film for film in filmSelect if film[0] not in remove]\n    \n    return filmList\n#endmethod",
      "execution_count": 44,
      "outputs": []
    },

      "metadata": {
        "_uuid": "fa15a28e6661c6d174b04545d859a85a84d36b7e"

      "cell_type": "markdown",
      "source": "The following function is the **Main function** that will create a list of 5 films that will be recommended to the user."
    },
    {
      "metadata": {
        "_cell_guid": "04fed780-b172-4273-bce1-a32154f99975",
        "_uuid": "77fb1486502bc047a04ffe7f5f38c2dc080b4d8c",

      },
      "cell_type": "code",
      "source": "def findSimilar(df, idEntry, delSequel = True, verbose = False):\n    if verbose:\n        print(90*'_' + '\\n' + \"Query: Films similar to id = {}  -> '{}'\".format(idEntry, df.iloc[idEntry]['movie_title']))\n    #endif\n    #Recommend films\n    listRecommend = recommend(df, idEntry)\n    \n    #Create list of 31 films\n    paraList = extractParameters(df, listRecommend)\n    \n    #Select 5 films from the list\n    filmSelect = []\n    filmSelect = addToSelection(filmSelect, paraList)\n    \n    #Delete Sequels\n    if delSequel: filmSelect = removeSequel(filmSelect)\n    #endif\n    \n    #Add new films to complete the list\n    filmSelect = addToSelection(filmSelect, paraList)\n    \n    selectTitle = []\n    for i, s in enumerate(filmSelect):\n        selectTitle.append([s[0].replace(u'\\xa0', u''), s[5]])\n        if verbose: print(\"no{:<2}     -> {:<30}\".format(i + 1, s[0]))\n        #endif\n    #endfor\n    \n    return selectTitle\n#endmethod",

      "cell_type": "markdown",
      "source": "**Making actual recommendations**\n\nWhile building the recommendation engine, we are quickly faced to a big issue: the existence of sequels make that some recommendations may seem quite dumb. As an exemple, somebody who enjoyed \"Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man's Chest\" would probably not like to be adviced to watch this:"

      "metadata": {
        "_uuid": "d2c536c5ac04df74d3a16aeda617e7925232b596"
      },
      "cell_type": "markdown",
      "source": "The current engine is built in such a fashion that it is quite probable that if the engine matches one film of a series (like a trilogy), it will end recommending various of them. In the previous example, we see that the engine recommends the three films of the **Pirates of the Caribbean trilogy** majorly. \nHence, we tried to find a way to prevent that kind of behaviour and I concluded that the quickest way to do it would be to work on the film's titles. To do so, I used the **fuzzywuzzy** package to build the **removeSequels** function. This function defines the degree of similarity of two film titles and if too close, the most recent film is removed from the list of recommendations. Using this function on the previous exemple, we end with the following recommendations:"
    },
